TITLE: Mangusta 80 vs Smaller Charter Yachts in Marbella: Why 24 m Changes the Day
DESCRIPTION: Mangusta 80 (24 m, 12 guests, free jet ski) vs the 15–18 m luxury yachts typically chartered in Marbella. Honest comparison on deck space, water toys, range and cost-per-person.

Home › Guide › Mangusta 80 vs Smaller Charter Yachts in Marbella: Why 24 m Changes the Day By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers The Mangusta 80 — our "Nina" — is a 24 m Italian sport yacht in service since 2020 and the biggest yacht regularly available for day charter from Puerto Banús. This page is the honest comparison vs the 15-18 m "luxury" yachts most Marbella charter brokers will steer you towards, with a free jet ski thrown in. The Marbella luxury-yacht segment below 24 m When you ask any Marbella broker for a "luxury yacht charter", you typically get pitched in this size class: Princess V58 / V60 — 18 m British sport cruiser, 10 day guests, single helm, no jet ski standard. Sunseeker Predator 60 / Manhattan 60 — 18 m sport-cruiser/flybridge, 10-12 day guests, premium fit-out. Azimut 55 Fly / 60 Fly — 17-18 m Italian flybridge, 10-12 day guests, large flybridge. Pershing 56 / 62 — 17-19 m Italian high-performance, sleek interior, 10-12 day guests. Galeon 500 Fly / 560 — 16-17 m Polish flybridge with side terraces, 10-12 day guests. All beautiful boats. All charter in Marbella between €3,500 and €5,500 for a 4-hour half-day. All are 17-19 m and 10-12 guest capacity. The Mangusta 80 sits one full size class above. At 24 metres / 80 feet , she has roughly 50% more deck and interior volume than a 17 m Sunseeker. And she comes with a free Sea-Doo jet ski on the swim platform. Deck space — the most tangible difference A 17 m yacht has roughly 65 m² of usable deck (cockpit + flybridge + foredeck combined). The Mangusta 80 has roughly 120 m² . Concretely: Bow: two full-width sun-pads vs one sun-pad split for a windlass on the smaller yachts. Cockpit: dining for 12 vs dining for 8 cramped. Aft deck: bench seating + table + tender garage opening with the jet ski underneath. Side decks: walk-around access vs side-mounted on smaller sport cruisers. Sun-pad/lounge total: sleeps 6 in sun at once vs 4 on the smaller yachts. The jet ski — €800 of value, free Every other luxury yacht charter in Marbella charges €200/h for jet ski rental as an extra (often a separate booking with a separate captain). On the Mangusta 80, the Sea-Doo is on the swim platform, ready to launch, free for guests to use throughout the entire charter. Over a 4-hour booking, that's typically €800 of jet-ski rental value baked in. Crew — captain alone vs captain + deckhand The smaller 17 m yachts run with one captain. The Mangusta 80 needs two crew (captain + deckhand) for safe handling at 24 m — and the deckhand becomes your service person too: drinks served, water toys deployed, swim platform manoeuvres handled. The smaller yachts can't match this without paying extra for a hostess. Cabins and overnight Boat Cabins Overnight guests Chef-grade galley Princess V58 2 4 No (compact galley) Sunseeker Predator 60 2 4 No Azimut 55 Fly 3 6 Compact Mangusta 80 3 6 Yes — full galley, marble worktop If overnight comfort matters, the Mangusta 80 has a proper master suite with king bed, plus two guest cabins, plus a saloon convertible — and a galley that can actually produce a cooked dinner, not just reheat. Range and offshore capability The Mangusta hull was designed for high-speed offshore work — twin diesels driving water jets, 30+ knot top speed, comfortable in seas that would stop a 15 m sport cruiser. For a Gibraltar day trip from Puerto Banús (100 NM round trip), the Mangusta does it in 7 hours of total time at planing speed. A 17 m yacht needs 9-10 hours and the captain looks at the forecast much more nervously. Cost — per guest on a full boat Boat Half-day 4h (peak) Guests Per person Princess V58 ~€3,500 10 €350 Sunseeker Predator 60 ~€4,200 12 €350 Pershing 56 ~€4,500 10 €450 Mangusta 80 €4,719 12 €393 (incl. jet ski + 8 extra metres of boat) On a full charter, the Mangusta works out to within €50 per person of a 17 m alternative — and you're getting 50% more boat plus the free jet ski. When the Mangusta 80 is the obvious pick Big celebration days — birthdays, anniversaries, milestone events. The deck space and crew service deliver the experience. Groups of 10-12 who want everyone to fit comfortably (not crammed on the cockpit). Guests who'll actually use the water toys. Jet ski + paddleboard + donut all included. Overnight on board — three cabins and a proper galley. Long-range trips — Gibraltar, multi-day to Cádiz, the offshore work where 17 m boats start feeling small. Compare across our fleet If 12-guest superyacht scale is overkill, our 12.5 m options sit at €749/2h — see the Astondoa 40 (9 guests, Spanish-built classic) and Azimut 39 (11 guests, Italian flybridge). For the full Mangusta 80 details, photos, gallery and the chef-platter video: Mangusta 80 page . Frequently asked questions What other 'luxury' yachts can I charter in Marbella? Mid-tier luxury segment from Puerto Banús typically runs 15-18 m: Princess V58, Sunseeker Predator 60, Azimut 55 Fly, Pershing 56. None are 24 m, none include a jet ski free, and most don't have the chef-grade galley layout the Mangusta has. Is the Mangusta 80 really the biggest charter yacht in Marbella? For day charter from Puerto Banús, yes — at 24 m she's the largest yacht regularly bookable for a day or half-day on the Marbella stretch. Bigger yachts (30 m+ Sunseekers, 40 m Benettis) berth in Puerto Banús but are private or full-week charter only. What's the cost difference between Mangusta and a typical 16 m luxury yacht? A 16 m Princess V60 charter runs ~€3,500-€4,500 for 4 hours. Our Mangusta 80 is €4,719 for the same 4 hours — €200-€1,200 more, but you get 8 m more boat, a free jet ski (€800 of value), captain + deckhand crew, full galley and three real cabins. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

TITLE: Mangusta 80 vs Sunseeker Predator 74: Which Superyacht Wins in Marbella?
DESCRIPTION: Mangusta 80 vs Sunseeker Predator 74 Marbella: compare size, capacity, amenities &amp; price. Find out which superyacht wins for your charter day. Book now.

Home › Guide › Mangusta 80 vs Sunseeker Predator 74: Which Superyacht Wins in Marbella? By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers When planning a luxury day on the Costa del Sol, few decisions are as important as choosing the right boat. Two of the most sought-after superyachts in Marbella are the Mangusta 80 and the Sunseeker Predator 74 . Both turn heads in Puerto Banús, but they offer very different experiences. In this Mangusta 80 vs Sunseeker Predator 74 Marbella comparison, we break down size, speed, capacity, amenities, and price to help you decide which superyacht wins for your charter day. Size and Capacity The Mangusta 80 measures 24 metres (79 ft) and can carry up to 12 passengers. The Sunseeker Predator 74 is slightly shorter at 22.5 metres (74 ft) and typically also carries 12 passengers. The Mangusta has a wider beam (5.5m vs 5.2m), giving it more deck space for lounging and dining. If you're a group of 10-12, the Mangusta offers more room to spread out, especially on the flybridge and aft deck. Speed and Performance The Sunseeker Predator 74 is built for speed. With twin MAN V12 engines (1,550 hp each), it can reach a top speed of 38-40 knots. The Mangusta 80, powered by twin MTU 16V 2000 M93 engines, tops out at around 32 knots and cruises comfortably at 28 knots. For pure adrenaline, the Predator wins. But the Mangusta's cruising speed is more than enough for a relaxed day hopping between Marbella's best anchorages like Cala del Faro and Cala Cortés. Design and Layout The Mangusta 80 is a classic Italian open sport yacht with sleek lines and a spacious flybridge. Its layout includes a large aft deck with a dining table, a forward sunpad, and a well-appointed saloon. The Sunseeker Predator 74 has a more aggressive, sporty profile with a lower profile and a cockpit that feels like a sports car. The Predator's interior is more modern and minimalist, while the Mangusta feels more traditional and luxurious. Onboard Amenities Both boats come with a licensed skipper, fuel, insurance, and a full drinks package (water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava) plus light snacks. The Mangusta 80 goes a step further by including a jet ski free of charge for the minimum 4-hour booking. The Predator does not typically include a jet ski. For entertainment, the Mangusta has a high-end sound system, while the Predator focuses more on the driving experience. Charter Pricing Our Mangusta 80 (available in grey and white) starts at €4,719 for a minimum of 4 hours. This includes the jet ski, skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, and VAT. The Sunseeker Predator 74 is not in our fleet, so pricing is on request from other operators. Expect to pay a similar or higher rate, often without inclusions like a jet ski. For the best value, the Mangusta 80 is hard to beat. Which Boat Is Best for Your Group? Choose the Mangusta 80 if you want a spacious, luxurious day with a jet ski included, ideal for families or groups of friends who want to relax and have fun. Choose the Sunseeker Predator 74 if you're a speed enthusiast who prioritises performance and a sporty aesthetic. For most charterers in Marbella, the Mangusta's combination of space, amenities, and price makes it the winner. Where Will You Cruise? Both boats depart from Puerto Banús , Marbella's iconic superyacht marina. Popular routes include heading east to Cabopino and Marbella Marina , or west to Estepona and Sotogrande . Anchor at Cala del Faro or Cala Cortés for swimming in crystal-clear waters. The Mangusta's shallow draft (1.2m) allows it to get closer to shore than the Predator (1.5m). For more ideas, browse our Marbella boat rental guide . Final Verdict In the Mangusta 80 vs Sunseeker Predator 74 Marbella showdown, the winner depends on your priorities. The Mangusta offers more space, a jet ski, and a better all-inclusive price. The Predator offers more speed and a sportier look. For a day of luxury, fun, and value on the Costa del Sol, the Mangusta 80 takes the crown. Check availability and book your Mangusta 80 charter today . Frequently Asked Questions Which is bigger: Mangusta 80 or Sunseeker Predator 74? The Mangusta 80 is 24m long, while the Sunseeker Predator 74 is 22.5m. The Mangusta has a slightly larger beam and more deck space, making it better for groups wanting to spread out. Both can carry up to 12 passengers. Which boat is faster in Marbella waters? The Sunseeker Predator 74 is typically faster, with a top speed around 38-40 knots thanks to its sportier hull and twin MAN engines. The Mangusta 80 cruises at 28-30 knots, but its top speed is around 32 knots. For pure adrenaline, the Predator wins. Can I charter a Sunseeker Predator 74 in Marbella? Yes, you can charter a Sunseeker Predator 74 in Marbella, but it is not in our fleet. We offer the Mangusta 80 (grey and white) and other superyachts. For a Predator, you would need to contact other operators. What is included in the Mangusta 80 charter? The Mangusta 80 charter includes a licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, safety equipment, and Spanish IVA (21%). A jet ski is also included free for the minimum 4-hour booking. How much does the Mangusta 80 cost to charter? The Mangusta 80 starts at €4,719 for a minimum of 4 hours. This includes the jet ski. For longer durations, pricing is on request. All prices include VAT, skipper, fuel, drinks, and snacks. Which boat is better for a party in Puerto Banús? The Mangusta 80 has a larger flybridge and aft deck, making it ideal for socialising and parties. The Sunseeker Predator 74 is more focused on speed and sporty lines. For a party, the Mangusta's spacious layout wins. Can I visit Cala del Faro or Cala Cortés with either boat? Yes, both boats can anchor at Cala del Faro and Cala Cortés. The Mangusta's shallow draft (approx 1.2m) allows it to get closer to the beach. The Predator's deeper draft may require a bit more distance, but both are fine for those spots. Which boat is more luxurious? Both are high-end superyachts, but the Mangusta 80 offers a more traditional Italian luxury feel with teak decks and spacious saloons. The Sunseeker Predator 74 has a more modern, sporty interior. It's a matter of taste. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

Marbella Art Fair 2026: dates, location & highlights The Marbella Art Fair 2026 takes place at the Palacio de Ferias y Congresos (Marbella Exhibition Centre), Avenida José Meliá. Opening hours are 10:00–21:00 daily . The fair features modern and contemporary art from Spanish and international galleries, with a strong focus on painting, sculpture, and photography. Entry tickets are available on-site or online. The venue is a 6 km drive from Puerto Banús — roughly 15 minutes by taxi. Why add a yacht charter to your art fair visit? A Marbella art fair yacht charter turns a single event into a full-day experience. Start the morning browsing galleries, then head to Puerto Banús for an afternoon on the water. Cruise past the Golden Mile mansions, anchor at Cala del Faro for a swim, or simply enjoy the views of La Concha mountain from the flybridge. TITLE: Marbella Skipper &amp; Captain Tipping Etiquette Guide
DESCRIPTION: Learn marbella skipper tipping etiquette for your boat charter. Our guide covers how much to tip (€50-€200), when, and who to tip. Plan your day now.

Home › Guide › Marbella Skipper & Captain Tipping Etiquette Guide By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Planning a boat charter in Marbella? Understanding marbella skipper tipping etiquette ensures you enjoy a smooth, respectful experience on the water. Whether you're renting a luxury yacht from Puerto Banús or a speedboat for a day trip, knowing how much to tip, when, and who to tip is key. This guide covers all the numbers and local customs you need. Why tipping your skipper matters Your skipper is responsible for navigation, safety, and making your day unforgettable—from anchoring at Cala del Faro to spotting dolphins off Cabopino. A tip shows appreciation for their expertise and effort. It's not mandatory, but it's a standard courtesy in the yachting world. Most skippers work on a base salary plus tips, so your gesture directly supports their livelihood. How much to tip: concrete numbers A good rule is 10-15% of the charter cost. Here's what that looks like for our boats: Tier A boats (e.g., Astondoa 40, Azimut 39): €749 for 2 hours → tip €75-€110. For a full day (€2,299), tip €200-€300. Tier B boats (e.g., Mangusta 80, white or grey): €4,719 for 4 hours → tip €400-€700. This includes a free jet ski, so tip higher if you use it. Other boats (e.g., Ferretti 94, Pershing 46): pricing on request, but tip 10-15% of the total. For shorter trips (2 hours), €50-€80 is fine. For full-day charters (8 hours), €150-€300 is typical. Who to tip and how On most charters, you only tip the skipper. If there's a deckhand or stewardess (common on larger yachts like the Canados 86 or Ferretti 94), tip them separately. A fair split: 70% to skipper, 30% to crew. Hand cash directly to each person at the end of the trip. Avoid leaving tips on the table or in an envelope—it's more personal this way. Cash is king: what to bring Always bring euros in cash. Most skippers don't carry card machines, and ATMs in Puerto Banús can have long queues. If you're on a Mangusta 80 and want to tip for the jet ski, bring extra. For a group of 10-12 people, pooling cash beforehand makes it easy. A typical envelope of €200-€300 works for a half-day charter. When not to tip If the skipper is late, rude, or doesn't follow the agreed itinerary (e.g., skipping Cala Cortés without reason), you're not obliged to tip. You can also mention any issues to us—we take feedback seriously. Poor service is rare, but it happens. Trust your instincts. Cultural nuances in Marbella Marbella is international, but Spanish tipping culture is relaxed. 10% is considered generous. Unlike the US, you won't be chased for a tip. A friendly 'gracias' and a handshake are always appreciated. If you're unsure, ask the skipper discreetly—they'll likely say 'whatever you think is fair'. That's a polite cue to tip the standard amount. Frequently asked questions How much should I tip the skipper on a Marbella boat charter? A standard tip is 10-15% of the charter cost. For a half-day (4 hours) on a Tier A boat like the Azimut 39 (€749/2h or €2,299/8h), a €50-€100 tip is common. For a full-day on a Mangusta 80 (€4,719/4h), consider €200-€300. Always adjust based on service quality. Is tipping expected on boat charters in Marbella? Tipping is not mandatory but is highly appreciated. Skippers and crew work hard to ensure a safe, enjoyable trip. Many guests tip as a gesture of thanks, especially if the skipper goes above and beyond—e.g., finding secluded coves or providing great local knowledge. Should I tip in cash or by card? Cash is always best. Most skippers prefer euros, but some may accept other currencies. Card tips are rarely possible on board. Bring enough cash for the tip plus any extras you might want (e.g., jet ski hire on the Mangusta 80). Do I tip the skipper and the crew separately? Yes, if you have a separate deckhand or stewardess, tip them individually. A common split is 70% to the skipper, 30% to the crew. For example, on a €2,000 charter, €140 to skipper, €60 to crew. Hand each person their tip directly. What if the service is poor—should I still tip? No, you are never obliged to tip for poor service. If the skipper was rude, unsafe, or didn't deliver the promised itinerary, skip the tip. You can also mention any issues to your booking contact; we take feedback seriously. When is the right time to give the tip? At the end of the charter, after you've docked and before you leave the boat. Hand the cash to the skipper with a handshake and a thank you. This is a polite, professional moment. Avoid tipping during the trip as it can feel awkward. Does the charter price include gratuity? No, our prices include skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, insurance, and VAT, but not tips. The price you see (e.g., €749 for 2 hours on the Astondoa 40) is the total; tips are extra. This is standard across Marbella charters. Are there any cultural tips for tipping in Marbella? Marbella is a cosmopolitan area, but Spanish tipping culture is modest. Unlike the US, 10% is generous. Don't feel pressured to overtip. A simple 'gracias' with a smile goes a long way. If you're unsure, ask the skipper discreetly—they'll appreciate the thought. ★★★★★ 4.9 · verified reviews From €749 2h skippered charter Instant quotes from local operators across Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, Cabopino, Estepona & Sotogrande. 💬 Message on WhatsApp Avg reply < 5 min · No deposit until you confirm 📅 Book now Browse the full fleet → All charters include Licensed skipper & fuel Drinks: water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava Light snacks Insurance & safety equipment Snorkel gear & inflatables VAT 21% — no surprises

TITLE: Plan a Family Boat Day from Cabopino: Snorkeling, Beaches &amp; Tips
DESCRIPTION: Plan a family boat day from Cabopino, Marbella. Snorkeling, beach stops &amp; tips for 2025. From €749 for 2h with skipper, drinks &amp; VAT included.

Home › Guide › Plan a Family Boat Day from Cabopino: Snorkeling, Beaches & Tips By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Planning a family boat day from Cabopino is one of the best ways to enjoy the Costa del Sol with kids. Cabopino’s sandy beach, protected dunes and clear waters make it an ideal base for a half-day or full-day charter. Our fleet departs from nearby Puerto Banús (just 5 minutes by car), and we offer family-friendly boats starting at €749 for 2 hours, with a licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks and VAT included. Here’s everything you need to know to plan your day: snorkeling spots, beach stops, boat options and practical tips. Why choose Cabopino for a family boat day? Cabopino is quieter than Marbella’s Golden Mile beaches, with a natural dune system and shallow waters that are safe for children. The marina has a small harbour with a restaurant and parking. From the water, you can anchor off Cabopino Beach (Playa de Cabopino) or explore nearby coves like Cala del Faro and Cala Cortés. The sea here is often calmer than further west, making it a good choice for families with young kids. Average water temperatures in summer reach 24–26°C. Our family-friendly boats departing from Puerto Banús All our charters depart from Puerto Banús Marina, a 5-minute drive from Cabopino. For families, we recommend these boats: Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 pax) – €749/2h or €2,299/8h. Spacious cockpit, sunpad, and a small cabin for changing. Azimut 39 (12.5m, 11 pax) – same pricing. Flybridge option for shade and views. Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) – €4,719 minimum 4h, includes a free jet ski. Ideal for larger families or multi-family groups. Smaller groups (up to 5 pax) can use the Dubhe (8m) or Mariah SX21 (6.4m) – pricing on request via WhatsApp. Every charter includes a licensed skipper, fuel, water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava, light snacks, insurance, safety equipment and Spanish IVA (21%). No hidden fees. Snorkeling spots near Cabopino The coastline between Cabopino and Marbella has several good snorkeling locations. Our skippers know the best spots based on wind and tide: Cala del Faro – rocky seabed with bream, wrasse and occasional octopus. Depth 3–6m. Cala Cortés – sheltered cove with clear water and sandy patches. Good for beginners. Cabopino reef – just off the beach, shallow (1–3m) and safe for young children. We provide snorkeling masks and fins on request. Bring your own if you prefer. Water visibility is typically 10–20m in summer. Beach stops and anchor points You can anchor for a swim stop, have lunch on board, or go ashore at these beaches: Playa de Cabopino – fine sand, dunes, chiringuito (beach bar). Shallow entry. Playa de Artola – quieter, with natural dunes and fewer crowds. Playa del Alicate – long stretch of sand, good for walking. Playa de Calahonda – further east, with rocky areas for snorkeling. Your skipper will anchor in a spot that suits your group. If you want to go ashore, they’ll drop you by tender (small dinghy) if the boat is too large to beach. What to bring for a family boat day Pack light and smart. Essentials include swimsuits, towels, sunscreen (SPF 50+, reef-safe), hats, sunglasses, and a light jacket for the afternoon breeze. TITLE: Marbella Boat Rental in June: Weather, Sea Conditions &amp; Tips
DESCRIPTION: Discover marbella boat rental weather june conditions: 25°C, 21°C sea temp, 9h sun, calm seas. Book your charter in Puerto Banús with skipper &amp; drinks included.

Home › Guide › Marbella Boat Rental in June: Weather, Sea Conditions & Tips By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers June is arguably the sweet spot for a marbella boat rental weather june conditions: warm air, pleasant sea temperatures, long sunny days, and minimal wind. With average highs of 29°C, sea temperatures of 21°C, and 9 hours of daily sunshine, the Mediterranean off Puerto Banús is at its most inviting. Whether you're planning a family day out, a group celebration, or a romantic sunset cruise, this guide covers everything you need to know – from sea conditions and wind patterns to booking tips and the best boats for the month. June Weather Averages for Marbella June in Marbella delivers consistently good weather. Historical data shows average daytime highs of 29°C, with overnight lows around 19°C. Sea temperature reaches 21°C by mid-month – warm enough for extended swimming without a wetsuit. Rainfall is minimal (3-4 days total), and humidity is moderate at 60-65%. The sun rises around 07:00 and sets after 21:30, giving you over 14 hours of daylight. For boaters, the key metric is wind. The prevailing Poniente (westerly) wind blows at 10-15 knots in June, creating a gentle chop of 0.3-0.6m in the open sea but calm conditions close to shore. The Levante (easterly) is rare in June, meaning you're unlikely to encounter the stronger winds that can affect autumn charters. Water visibility often exceeds 15 metres, especially near the coves east of Marbella. Sea Conditions & Best Times to Go The Mediterranean along the Costa del Sol is generally calm in June. The coastline from Puerto Banús to Estepona offers sheltered waters, while heading east towards Cabopino and Cala del Faro gives you slightly more exposed but still manageable conditions. Our skippers know the local microclimates – they'll adjust the route based on the day's forecast. For the smoothest ride, morning charters (10:00-14:00) typically have the calmest seas. Afternoons can see a light thermal breeze pick up, but it rarely exceeds 15 knots. Sunset charters (16:00-21:00) are popular for the golden light and cooler temperatures – the sea often remains flat until dusk. What to Wear & Pack for a June Boat Charter Daytime: swimwear, shorts, t-shirt, sunglasses, and a hat. Sunscreen SPF 50 is essential – the reflection off the water intensifies UV exposure. We provide towels on all charters. For the evening return, pack a light jumper or windbreaker as the temperature can drop to 19°C after sunset, and the boat's movement creates a wind chill. Non-slip shoes are recommended but not mandatory – barefoot is fine on deck. Don't forget a camera or phone for the views of La Concha mountain and the Marbella skyline. If you're prone to seasickness, consider taking a preventative antihistamine an hour before departure – though with June's calm seas, it's rarely needed. Best Boats for June Charters Our fleet of 15+ boats departing from Puerto Banús includes options for every group size and budget. For June, we recommend: Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 pax) – Tier A pricing: €749/2h to €2,299/8h. Great value, spacious cockpit, and a bow sundeck for soaking up the June sun. Azimut 58 Flybridge (17.6m, 12 pax) – The flybridge offers shaded seating for those who want to escape the midday heat while still enjoying panoramic views. Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) – Available in grey and white variants. Minimum 4h at €4,719, includes a free jet ski – perfect for June water sports. Ferretti 94 (29m, 12 pax) – Our largest yacht, ideal for luxury celebrations with ample indoor and outdoor space. Speedboat (7m, 6 pax) – For a more adventurous, wind-in-your-hair experience. Priced on request. All charters include a licensed skipper, fuel, drinks (water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava), light snacks, insurance, and Spanish VAT. No hidden fees. Itinerary Ideas for June With 9 hours of daylight, you can tailor your route. Popular June itineraries include: Puerto Banús to Cala del Faro (east): 30 minutes from base. Swim in turquoise waters, then anchor near the cliffs for lunch. Return via the Marbella coastline. Puerto Banús to Estepona (west): 45 minutes. Stop at the fishing port for fresh seafood, then explore the quieter coves near Bahía de Estepona. Sunset cruise to Cabopino: Depart at 17:00, cruise east, drop anchor for a swim, then watch the sun set behind La Concha while enjoying cava. Full-day to Sotogrande: 1.5 hours each way. Visit the upscale marina, have lunch at a beach club, and return via the coast. Your skipper will advise on the best option based on wind and sea conditions on the day. Booking Tips for June June is the start of the high season in Marbella. We recommend booking 2-3 weeks in advance, especially for weekends and popular boats like the Mangusta 80 or Azimut 58. Weekday availability is generally better. For the best value, consider a 4-hour charter (€1,299 for Tier A boats) which gives you enough time for a swim stop and coastal cruise without committing to a full day. TITLE: Best Time of Day for Dolphin Watching in Marbella
DESCRIPTION: Discover the best time for dolphin watching Marbella. Morning or sunset? We share concrete tips, boat options, and departure info from Puerto Banús.

Home › Guide › Best Time of Day for Dolphin Watching in Marbella By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Marbella's coastline is one of the best places in the Mediterranean to spot dolphins in the wild. But the question we hear most often is: what is the best time for dolphin watching in Marbella? The short answer is early morning, but sunset runs are a close second. In this guide, we break down the pros and cons of each time slot, share concrete tips, and show you which boats from our fleet are best for the job. Why Morning Trips (8–10 AM) Are the Best Time for Dolphin Watching in Marbella Dolphins are most active during the early hours. They feed in the morning, and the sea is usually calmer before the afternoon wind picks up. Calm water means better visibility and a smoother ride. From Puerto Banús, most dolphin zones are just 20–30 minutes away, so a 2-hour charter is plenty. Our Boat Rental Marbella fleet includes the Astondoa 40 and Azimut 39 (both Tier A, €749 for 2 hours) — ideal for a quick, productive morning trip. Sunset Dolphin Watching (6–8 PM): The Photographer's Choice Sunset trips are popular for a reason: golden light, cooler temperatures, and a relaxed vibe. From June to September, the sun sets around 9 PM, so a 6–8 PM slot gives you both good light and a higher chance of sightings. Dolphins are still active, though slightly less than in the morning. The Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) is a fantastic option for a sunset charter, offering plenty of deck space and a free jet ski. Rates start at €4,719 for 4 hours. Afternoon Trips: Possible but Less Reliable Between 12 PM and 4 PM, the sea is often choppier, and boat traffic is at its peak. Dolphin sightings are still possible — especially if you head further out — but the encounter rate drops. If you're set on an afternoon trip, stick to a 2–3 hour window and book a boat with a flybridge for better visibility, like the Azimut 58 Flybridge (17.6m, 12 pax). Pricing is on request via WhatsApp. Best Months for Dolphin Watching in Marbella While dolphins are present year-round, the best months are May through October . During this period, calm sea days are more frequent, and encounter rates reach 85–90%. Winter months (November–February) see fewer sightings due to rougher seas and shorter daylight hours. For a full overview of what to expect, read our Marbella dolphin watching guide . Which Boats Are Best for Dolphin Watching? Check the weather — calm seas (Beaufort scale 0–2) give the best odds. Bring a camera — sunrise and sunset light make for stunning shots. Frequently Asked Questions What is the best time of day for dolphin watching in Marbella? Early morning (8–10 AM) is generally the best time for dolphin watching in Marbella. The sea is calmest, dolphins are actively feeding, and there is less boat traffic. Sunset trips (6–8 PM) are a close second, offering better lighting and cooler conditions, especially in summer. Can you see dolphins in the afternoon in Marbella? Yes, but afternoon sightings are less reliable due to increased boat traffic and choppier waters, particularly from May to September. If you go, choose a 2–3 hour window between 2 PM and 5 PM. Our Tier A boats like the Astondoa 40 are available for afternoon charters. Which months are best for dolphin watching in Marbella? May through October offer the highest encounter rates, often 85–90% on calm days. Dolphins are present year-round, but winter months (November–February) see fewer sightings due to rougher seas and shorter daylight hours. How long does a dolphin-watching trip from Puerto Banús take? Most dolphin-watching trips last 2 to 4 hours. The dolphin zones are typically 20–30 minutes from Puerto Banús, leaving plenty of time for observation. Our Tier A boats (Astondoa 40, Azimut 39) are ideal for 2-hour trips starting at €749. What types of dolphins can I see in Marbella? The most common species are bottlenose dolphins and striped dolphins. Occasionally, you may spot short-beaked common dolphins. They are often seen in pods of 5–20 individuals, sometimes larger. Is it better to go dolphin watching in the morning or at sunset? Morning trips (8–10 AM) offer the highest probability of sightings due to calm seas and active feeding. Sunset trips (6–8 PM) provide better light for photography and a more relaxed atmosphere. Both are excellent options. What should I bring for a dolphin-watching trip in Marbella? Bring sunscreen, a hat, sunglasses, a light jacket (especially for sunset), and a camera. TITLE: Marbella Tuna Fishing Season: When to Book Your Charter
DESCRIPTION: Plan your Marbella tuna fishing season charter with expert timing tips. Bluefin run June–October. Book your boat from Puerto Banús today.

Home › Guide › Marbella Tuna Fishing Season: When to Book Your Charter By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Marbella's tuna fishing season offers some of the best bluefin action in the Mediterranean. From June to October, the warm waters off Puerto Banús attract trophy-sized Atlantic bluefin tuna, drawing anglers from across Europe. Whether you're a seasoned fisherman or a first-timer, timing your charter right makes all the difference. This guide covers peak months, boat options, and everything you need to book your Marbella tuna fishing season charter. When Is the Marbella Tuna Fishing Season? The tuna fishing season in Marbella runs from June to October, with the peak in August and September. During these months, sea temperatures range from 20°C to 26°C, creating ideal conditions for bluefin tuna to feed near the coast. Early morning trips, departing around 7–8 AM, often see the most activity. Our fleet of 27 boats, all based in Puerto Banús, offers quick access to prime fishing grounds just 5–10 nautical miles offshore. Best Boats for Tuna Fishing Charters For tuna fishing, you want a boat with range, comfort, and deck space. Our top picks include the Azimut 58 Flybridge (17.6m, 12 pax) for its stable platform and flybridge visibility, and the Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) for luxury and speed. The Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 pax) is a more budget-friendly option at €749 for 2 hours or €2,299 for a full day. All charters include a licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, and insurance—no hidden extras. Where You'll Fish: Puerto Banús and Beyond All our charters depart from Puerto Banús, Marbella's glamorous marina. From here, you can reach fishing spots like the waters off Cabopino, Cala del Faro, or further south towards Estepona. The continental shelf drops sharply just a few miles out, creating a natural feeding ground for tuna. Your skipper will navigate based on real-time conditions, ensuring you're where the fish are. What to Expect on a Tuna Fishing Charter A typical tuna fishing charter lasts 4 to 8 hours. You'll find rod holders, a fighting chair on larger boats, and plenty of shade. Our skippers are experienced in bluefin techniques, including trolling with lures and live bait. All safety equipment and insurance are included. You can also arrange for catch cleaning and packing. For the full experience, consider a full-day charter—you'll have time to explore multiple spots and enjoy lunch on the water. Pricing and Booking Tips Our Tier A boats (Astondoa 40, Azimut 39) start at €749 for 2 hours or €2,299 for 8 hours, all inclusive. Tier B boats like the Mangusta 80 require a minimum 4-hour charter at €4,719, which includes a free jet ski. Other boats are priced on request. For peak season (August–September), book at least 2–4 weeks in advance. Contact us via WhatsApp to check availability and customise your trip. Browse our full fleet to see all options. Local Tips for a Successful Trip Bring sun protection, a hat, and polarised sunglasses—the Mediterranean sun is intense. Wear non-slip shoes, and pack a light jacket for early mornings. Most charters provide drinks and snacks, but you can bring your own food. If you're prone to seasickness, take medication an hour before departure. The waters off Marbella are generally calm in summer, with swells rarely exceeding 1 metre. Frequently Asked Questions When is the best time for tuna fishing in Marbella? The peak Marbella tuna fishing season runs from June through October. Bluefin tuna are most active in August and September when water temperatures are highest and baitfish are abundant. Early morning charters often yield the best catches. What types of tuna can I catch off Marbella? The primary target is Atlantic bluefin tuna, which can weigh over 200 kg. You may also encounter yellowfin and skipjack tuna, especially later in the season. Our experienced skippers know the best spots for each species. How long is a typical tuna fishing charter? Most tuna fishing charters from Puerto Banús last 4 to 8 hours. Half-day trips (4 hours) are popular for groups, while full-day charters (8 hours) allow more time to reach deeper grounds. All boats include a licensed skipper and full amenities. Do I need a fishing license? No, you don't need a personal license. Our charters include a licensed skipper who handles all permits and regulatory requirements. Just bring your enthusiasm and sun protection. What boats are available for tuna fishing? URL: https://boatrentalinmarbella.com/blog/marbella-half-day-morning-vs-afternoon/
TITLE: Half-Day Charter Marbella: Morning vs Afternoon
DESCRIPTION: Deciding between a Marbella half day morning vs afternoon charter? Compare sea conditions, light, dining, and sunset options for your 4-hour boat trip from Puerto Banús.

Home › Guide › Half-Day Charter Marbella: Morning vs Afternoon By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Choosing between a morning and afternoon half-day charter in Marbella can shape your entire experience on the water. Both slots offer distinct advantages—from calm seas and cooler air in the morning to golden light and warmer water in the afternoon. Whether you're planning a family outing, a group celebration, or a romantic escape, knowing the differences helps you book the right 4-hour window. Below, we break down the key factors to consider when deciding on your Marbella half day morning vs afternoon charter. Morning Half-Day Charter (10:00–14:00) Morning charters depart from Puerto Banús at 10:00 and return by 14:00. The sea is typically flat, the wind is light, and the coastline is quieter. This slot is ideal for guests who want a smooth ride, cooler temperatures, and the option to anchor for a swim or a picnic lunch at a cala like Cala del Faro or Cala Cortés . You'll have the coves mostly to yourself, and the light is excellent for photography without the harsh midday glare. A morning charter also leaves your afternoon free for other activities—shopping on the Golden Mile or lunch at a chiringuito in Cabopino . Afternoon Half-Day Charter (15:00–19:00) An afternoon half-day starts at 15:00 and finishes around 19:00, just as the sun begins to set. The water is warmer, making swimming more comfortable, and the later hours offer the famous Marbella sunset behind La Concha mountain. This slot is popular for groups wanting a lively atmosphere, with more boats anchored near beach clubs and coves. You can anchor off Estepona or Sotogrande for a swim, then enjoy cava and snacks as the sky turns orange. The return to Puerto Banús is often the highlight, with the marina lights reflecting on the water. Sea Conditions and Weather Mornings in Marbella are usually calm, with sea breezes picking up after noon. If you or your guests are prone to seasickness, a morning charter is the safer bet. Afternoons can have a light chop, but it's rarely uncomfortable and often welcome for cooling off. Summer temperatures range from 25°C in the morning to 30°C+ in the afternoon—bring sunscreen regardless. Swimming and Water Activities Water temperature is warmer in the afternoon (often 24–26°C in summer) compared to morning (22–24°C). If swimming is a priority, book the afternoon. Mornings are still perfectly swimmable, but the cooler water can be a shock. Both slots allow time for snorkelling, paddleboarding, or using the jet ski included on the Mangusta 80 (Tier B). Dining Options: Onboard or Ashore On a morning charter, you can anchor for a picnic lunch or dock at a beachfront restaurant in Cabopino or Marbella Marina . Afternoon charters work well for a late lunch onboard (15:00–16:00) followed by a sunset drink. Both include drinks and snacks—beer, cava, white wine, soft drinks, and water—so you can focus on the experience. Sunset and Photography If sunset is your priority, choose the afternoon slot. The golden hour from 18:00 to 19:00 provides stunning light for photos, especially with La Concha or the Strait of Gibraltar in the background. Morning light is crisp and clean, ideal for capturing the coastline without haze. Which Boats Are Available? Our fleet offers several options for half-day charters, all departing from Puerto Banús . Tier A boats— Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 pax) and Azimut 39 (12.5m, 11 pax)—cost €749/2h or €2,299/8h. Tier B boats like the Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) start at €4,719/4h and include a jet ski. For other boats (e.g., Ferretti 94 , Canados 86 , Pershing 46 ), pricing is on request via WhatsApp. All charters include a licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, snacks, insurance, and 21% VAT. Frequently asked questions What is the difference between a morning and afternoon half-day charter in Marbella? A morning half-day runs from 10:00 to 14:00, offering calm seas, cooler temperatures, and a quieter coastline. An afternoon half-day runs from 15:00 to 19:00, featuring warmer water for swimming, golden light, and the chance to watch the sunset over the Mediterranean. Which half-day is better for swimming: morning or afternoon? The afternoon is better for swimming because the sea has warmed up from the morning sun, and the air temperature is at its peak. Morning water is cooler, but still pleasant in summer (typically 22–24°C). Can I have lunch on a morning charter? Yes, you can bring your own picnic or arrange a catered lunch. Many guests anchor at Cala del Faro or Cabopino and enjoy a relaxed onboard meal. Alternatively, you can dock at a chiringuito for a sit-down lunch. Is the afternoon charter better for sunset views? Absolutely. An afternoon charter ending around 19:00 in summer lets you watch the sun dip behind La Concha mountain and the Strait of Gibraltar. It’s a popular time for photos and a glass of cava on the bow. Are sea conditions different between morning and afternoon? Yes. Mornings typically have flat seas and light winds, ideal for smooth cruising. Afternoons can see a light thermal breeze and slight chop, but this is rarely uncomfortable and often welcomed for cooling off. Which time slot is less crowded on the water? Morning charters are quieter, with fewer boats and less activity in coves like Cala Cortés. Afternoons are busier, especially near popular anchorages and beach clubs, but the lively atmosphere is part of the appeal. Can I combine a half-day charter with a beach club visit? Yes, especially in the afternoon. You can anchor near a beach club like Ocean Club Marbella or Playa Padre, use the tender to go ashore, and return to your boat for a drink. Morning charters are better for a quiet swim and snorkel. What boats are available for a half-day charter? Our fleet includes the Astondoa 40 (12.5m, 9 pax) and Azimut 39 (12.5m, 11 pax) from €749/2h, and the Mangusta 80 (24m, 12 pax) from €4,719/4h. All depart from Puerto Banús. For other boats, pricing is on request via WhatsApp. Still unsure which slot suits you? Weather and Season Considerations In summer (June–September), sea temperatures average 24–26°C and winds are light in the morning. A half-day from 10:00 to 14:00 avoids the afternoon heat. A full-day from 10:00 to 18:00 lets you enjoy the calm morning, a lunch stop, and an afternoon swim. In spring or autumn, a half-day is often enough — the sun sets earlier and the water is cooler (18–22°C). What’s Included in Every Charter? TITLE: Marbella Yacht Charter VAT &amp; Tax: What You&#x27;ll Pay
DESCRIPTION: Understand marbella yacht charter VAT tax — Spanish IVA is always included in our prices. No hidden fees, 21% tax covered. Book with total transparency.

Home › Guide › Marbella Yacht Charter VAT & Tax: What You'll Pay By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers When you're planning a Marbella yacht charter , the last thing you want is a surprise tax bill at the end. That's why every price on our site includes Spanish IVA (VAT) at 21% — no hidden fees, no asterisks. Whether you're booking the €749/2h Astondoa 40 or the €4,719/4h Mangusta 80, what you see is exactly what you pay. This page explains how VAT works on yacht charters in Marbella, so you can book with total confidence. Spanish IVA on Yacht Charters: The Basics In Spain, all recreational boat charters are subject to a 21% Value Added Tax (IVA). This applies to any private charter departing from a Spanish port, including Puerto Banús, Marbella Marina, and Cabopino. The tax is calculated on the total charter fee, including the boat, skipper, fuel, and any included extras like drinks and snacks. Our prices are always quoted inclusive of IVA, so you don't need to do any mental arithmetic. For example, the €749/2h rate for the Azimut 39 already has the 21% tax baked in. This transparency is part of our commitment to honest, no-fluff service. What's Included in Our VAT-Inclusive Prices Every charter with us includes the following, all covered by the 21% IVA: Licensed skipper Fuel for the entire trip Water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, and cava Light snacks Insurance and safety equipment Spanish IVA (21%) — already included There are no additional port fees, cleaning charges, or tourist taxes. The price you see on our Marbella boat rental page is the final price. How IVA Affects Different Boat Tiers Our fleet is divided into pricing tiers, and IVA is included across all of them: Boat Price (IVA included) Duration Astondoa 40 €749 2 hours Azimut 39 €749 2 hours Mangusta 80 (any variant) €4,719 4 hours (min.) Other boats (e.g., Pershing 46, Ferretti 94) On request On request For boats like the Ferretti 94 or Canados 86, pricing is customised based on your itinerary. We'll provide a full quote via WhatsApp that includes IVA, so there are no surprises. Can You Reclaim IVA on a Yacht Charter? If you're an EU business with a valid VAT number, you may be able to reclaim the 21% IVA under Spanish reverse-charge rules. This typically applies to charters used for corporate entertainment or client meetings. Non-EU residents generally cannot reclaim IVA, as it's a consumption tax. We recommend speaking with your tax advisor to confirm eligibility. If you need an invoice with your VAT number, just let us know when booking via WhatsApp — we'll provide a proper tax receipt. No Tourist Tax or Hidden Surcharges Unlike some holiday destinations (e.g., the Balearic Islands), Marbella and the Costa del Sol do not impose a tourist tax on yacht charters. There are no municipal surcharges, port entry fees, or environmental taxes added to our prices. The 21% IVA is the only tax you'll pay. This makes chartering from Puerto Banús particularly straightforward. You can focus on enjoying the coastline — from the Golden Mile to Cala del Faro — without worrying about extra costs. What About Charters for Special Events? Whether you're booking a Marbella yacht charter for a birthday party, wedding reception, or corporate event, the same IVA rules apply. Our all-inclusive pricing covers everything, and we can tailor the catering, decorations, or entertainment to your needs. Just ask for a custom quote — it will always include IVA. For example, a 4-hour charter on the Mangusta 80 with a jet ski included costs €4,719, all taxes paid. No extra line items. Why We Include IVA in Our Prices We've been operating in Marbella long enough to know that hidden fees erode trust. By including IVA in every advertised price, we make budgeting simple. You don't need to calculate 21% on top of the quote — it's already there. This approach is consistent across our entire fleet, from the compact Dubhe (€ on request) to the 29m Ferretti 94. It's part of our ethos: honest, direct, and transparent. If you have any questions about taxes, just contact us — we're happy to explain. All prices listed on our site — from the €749/2h Astondoa 40 to the €4,719/4h Mangusta 80 — include Spanish IVA at 21%. There are no hidden taxes added at checkout. What is the VAT rate for yacht charters in Marbella? The standard Spanish IVA rate for recreational boat charters is 21%. This applies to all private charters departing from Puerto Banús and other Marbella marinas. Can I reclaim the VAT on my yacht charter? If you are an EU business with a valid VAT number, you may be able to reclaim the IVA under Spanish reverse-charge rules. Non-EU residents generally cannot reclaim. No. Fuel and a licensed skipper are included in every charter, and both are covered by the 21% IVA. You won't pay a cent more than the advertised price. TITLE: Cala de Mijas Music Festival: Yacht Charter from Marbella
DESCRIPTION: Cala de Mijas Music Festival 2026 by yacht from Marbella: 22 NM run, anchorage tips, fleet from €749/2h. Book via WhatsApp now.

Home › Guide › Cala de Mijas Music Festival: Yacht Charter from Marbella By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Cala de Mijas Music Festival turns a quiet stretch of Costa del Sol beach into one of the busiest weekends of the Andalucian summer — and the easiest way to attend without traffic, parking battles or queues is to arrive by sea. From Puerto Banús the run is roughly 22 nautical miles east, an hour at cruising speed, and you finish the day anchored offshore with the headline act drifting across the water. This guide explains how the trip actually works on our fleet, what it costs, and which boats suit the festival best. For the full boat list and pricing, see the main page . Why arrive at Cala de Mijas by yacht The festival site sits on the beachfront just east of La Cala de Mijas marina. On festival weekend the AP-7 exit backs up from late afternoon, taxis triple their fares and parking within 2 km is gone by 18:00. By yacht you bypass all of it: you anchor 200–300 metres off the beach, tender in when you want and tender out when you've had enough. You keep your own food, drinks and bathroom on board, and the return trip to Puerto Banús in flat night seas is genuinely one of the better parts of the day. Practically speaking, this is a charter that suits groups of 6–12 who want a proper day out rather than just transport. The boat is the venue; the festival is a 90-minute interval in the middle. The route from Puerto Banús All our boats depart Puerto Banús. The eastbound route runs past Marbella Marina, the Golden Mile, Río Verde, Cabopino and Calahonda before reaching La Cala de Mijas. Total distance is around 22 NM. A typical timeline on the Azimut 39 or Astondoa 40 at 22 knots: Time Location Notes 14:00 Depart Puerto Banús Welcome drinks, briefing 14:45 Cabopino Swim stop, 30–45 min 16:30 Arrive Cala de Mijas Anchor, tender check 17:00–22:00 Festival Tender shuttles ashore 22:30 Depart for Banús Dinner on deck 00:00 Back in Banús Late return possible The Mangusta 80 and Pershing 46 run the route noticeably faster, useful if you want a longer Cabopino stop. The Lagoon 380 catamaran is slower but the most stable platform at anchor off an open beach. Boats that suit the festival For groups of 8–11 the sweet spot is the Astondoa 40 or Azimut 39 — Tier A pricing, full inclusions, and enough deck space to actually enjoy the day. Both are 12.5m, both seat 9–11 guests, and both come in at €749 for 2 hours rising to €2,299 for 8 hours with skipper, fuel, drinks and 21% IVA included. For a statement event or a 12-guest party, the Mangusta 80 (white or grey) is the obvious upgrade: 24 metres, free jet ski, €4,719 minimum 4 hours. The Azimut 58 Flybridge, Pershing 46 and Ferretti 94 are priced on request via WhatsApp — useful if you want a flybridge for the sound system or extra cabins for guests staying late. For groups that prioritise stability over speed, the Lagoon 380 catamaran (11.6m, 10 pax) sits flat at anchor even in 1-metre swell. That matters at Cala de Mijas, which is an open roadstead. Anchoring and tender logistics The bay east of La Cala marina has a sand seabed in 6–10 metres, holding well in settled weather. We typically anchor 200–300 metres offshore — close enough for a 5-minute tender run, far enough to stay out of the swimming zone. The skipper runs a fixed shuttle: confirmed drop times (e.g. 17:00 and 19:30) and confirmed pickup times (e.g. 22:00 and midnight). You don't need to call — you just turn up at the agreed spot. Conditions matter. Westerly poniente winds above 15 knots make the anchorage uncomfortable; in that case the skipper will hold the boat closer to Cabopino, which is 6 NM back west and far more sheltered. We monitor the forecast 48 hours out and offer free date changes if conditions look unsuitable. The Mangusta 80 includes the jet ski free. For full inclusion details see the fleet page . Festival-day food on board Most groups skip the food trucks ashore and eat on deck. Standard catering is built into the price — light snacks for grazing through the afternoon. For a proper dinner we can add a chef-prepared menu (paella, grilled fish, salads) for €45–65 per person, ordered 72 hours in advance via WhatsApp. The 8-hour Tier A charter at €2,299 leaves comfortable headroom in most budgets for catering, festival tickets and a round of cocktails ashore. Booking timeline and deposits Cala de Mijas Music Festival weekend is the busiest non-July date for our fleet. Tier A boats and the Lagoon 380 sell out 4–6 weeks ahead. To book, message us on WhatsApp with date, group size and boat preference. We confirm within the hour during the working day, hold the slot for 24 hours, and send a deposit link — typically 30% to confirm, balance on the charter day. Cancellation for weather is free up to 48 hours before departure. The main page has the full fleet, current pricing and the WhatsApp button. Two scrolls and you're talking to the skipper. The run takes 50–70 minutes on a planing boat such as the Pershing 46 or Fairline Targa 12m, longer on a displacement cruiser. You stay on board for food, drinks and music drifting over the water, then tender ashore for the headline sets. The skipper coordinates timings so you don't miss the acts you care about. Plan the return for after sunset; the run back in flat evening seas is part of the experience. Which boats in your fleet work best for the festival? In settled summer weather, yes — the seabed is sand and holds well in 6–10 metres. The bay is an open roadstead though, so westerly poniente winds above 15 knots make it uncomfortable and the skipper may move the boat to a more sheltered spot near Cabopino. We monitor the forecast in the 48 hours before departure and will rebook your charter date free of charge if conditions look unsuitable. Safety always overrides the festival schedule. Evening Cruise Options After the Polo If you’ve booked a full-day charter, your skipper can take you from Puerto Banús to Estepona (10 NM west) or along the Golden Mile for sunset. The Azimut 58 Flybridge (17.6m, 12 pax) or Ferretti 94 (29m, 12 pax) are great for evening entertaining. For something smaller, the Speedboat (7m, 6 pax) is a fun option. All depart from Puerto Banús. Book Your Polo-Day Yacht Charter Ready to combine polo with a private yacht? Browse our full fleet and contact us via WhatsApp for availability. We recommend booking at least 2 weeks in advance during peak season (July–August). The Marbella Polo Cup usually runs from July to September – check the official dates. Frequently Asked Questions How far is Sotogrande from Puerto Banús? Sotogrande is about 30 nautical miles south of Marbella, or a 40–50 minute drive by car. The Santa María Polo Club is roughly 45 minutes from Puerto Banús Marina. What time do Marbella Polo Cup matches start? Matches at the Santa María Polo Club usually start at 16:00 and finish around 18:00, though times can vary by day. Check the official schedule before booking. Can I charter a yacht in the morning and still go to the polo? Yes. Charter a boat from 10:00 to 14:00, then drive to Sotogrande for the 16:00 match. You’ll be back in Puerto Banús by 18:30 for an evening cruise. Which boats are best for a polo-day itinerary? The Astondoa 40 (€749/2h) or Azimut 39 (€749/2h) work well for a short morning charter. For a longer day, the Mangusta 80 (from €4,719/4h) includes a jet ski. What’s included in the charter price? The yacht charter is for the morning or evening; you watch the match from the club’s grandstands. What’s the sunset time in Marbella during polo season? During summer (June–August), sunset is around 21:30. TITLE: Marbella Restaurants You Can Arrive at by Boat
DESCRIPTION: Marbella restaurants by boat: 9 beach clubs and chiringuitos with mooring or tender drop, plus 4h charter from €749. Book via WhatsApp today.

Home › Guide › Marbella Restaurants You Can Arrive at by Boat By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers The fastest table in Marbella is the one you reach by sea. Skip the N-340 traffic, the €25 valet and the 20-minute walk from the car park: arrive directly at the chiringuito by tender, or moor stern-to at a Puerto Banús quayside terrace. This guide covers nine restaurants between Estepona and Cabopino that work for a lunch stop on a half-day charter, the practicalities of getting ashore, and how to pair the meal with a swim at Cala del Faro or Río Verde . Puerto Banús quayside: mooring stern-to for lunch Five venues inside the marina take walk-up boat traffic from 12:00 to 16:00. Cipriani (Italian, terrace right on the Levante quay), Astral (Mediterranean fish, opposite the superyacht line), La Sala by the Sea (British-leaning brasserie, easy with kids), Pangea (steaks, lounge atmosphere) and Sumosan (Japanese, end of the harbour). All five sit within a 50m walk of the visitor berths. Our skipper calls Puerto Banús harbour control on VHF 09 about 30 minutes before arrival and you usually have a berth allocated by the time you tie up. Quayside rates for a 2-3 hour lunch run €40-€90 depending on overall length; for boats over 20m we pre-book the day before. None of these venues charge a corkage if you arrive by water — you simply order from their drinks list as usual. Trocadero Arena and the Río Verde anchorage Trocadero Arena sits 1.5NM east of Puerto Banús on the sand at Río Verde. It is the closest serious chiringuito to the marina and the easiest first stop on a 4h Tier A charter at €749. We anchor in 4-5m of water about 100m off the beach, drop the tender, and you step ashore at the lifeguard tower. The kitchen runs a Mediterranean menu: grilled sea bass €32, ibérico croquettes €18, rice dishes from €28 for two. Sunbeds on their stretch of sand cost €40 a pair including a parasol. Service from 13:30; reserve the morning of your charter on +34 952 779 365. From the anchorage you see La Concha and the Golden Mile framing the coast — one of the best lunch views in Marbella. Nikki Beach: the dressy option Nikki Beach Marbella sits 3NM east of Puerto Banús, in front of the Don Carlos hotel. The anchorage is exposed to the east wind, so we check the forecast and only commit if Levante stays under 12 knots. Tender ashore is a 4-minute run. The dress code matters here: no swimwear at the table after 14:00, so guests change on the boat into linen or a dress before the tender shuttle. A two-course lunch with a bottle of rosé runs €70-€110 a head; sunbeds €60 each. Sunday brunches are theatrical and pricey but a good reason to take the 8h charter at €2,299 and stay for the dancing-on-tables 16:00 set. Cabopino chiringuitos: low-key and fish-led Push another 5NM east of Nikki Beach and you reach the dune system at Cabopino. Three chiringuitos work here for a boat lunch: Bono Beach , Andy's Beach and El Oasis . All three are sand-floored, swimwear-OK, with main courses €18-€28 and a kids' menu around €14. Anchorage is sheltered from westerlies and the holding is good in 4m of sand. We drop the hook 120m off Bono Beach's lifeguard post and shuttle in by tender. This is the best stop if you want a quiet lunch without the Puerto Banús showboat energy; it also pairs nicely with a return swim at Cala Cortés on the way back . How the catering-onboard option works If you would rather not go ashore, every charter already includes water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava and light snacks — that is enough for a 2-3 hour trip. For a proper meal onboard we coordinate with you the day before: tapas platters from €18 per person, sushi boxes around €35, paella for the table at €45 per head. We collect the order from Puerto Banús before you board and serve it at anchor in your chosen cove. Drinks remain included on top. This is a good move on August weekends when the popular chiringuitos run two-hour waits for walk-ins. Recommended routes by charter length Charter length Route Lunch stop Price (Tier A) 2h Puerto Banús quay loop Cipriani or Astral, stern-to €749 4h Puerto Banús → Río Verde → return Trocadero Arena, tender ashore €1,499 6h Puerto Banús → Nikki Beach → Cala del Faro swim Nikki Beach (smart-casual) €1,899 8h Puerto Banús → Cabopino → sunset return Bono Beach, swimwear €2,299 All four routes run on Tier A boats (Astondoa 40 or Azimut 39, both 12.5m, up to 9-11 guests). Upgrading to a Mangusta 80 for the day starts at €4,719 for 4h and adds a free jet ski, which makes the swim stop between courses considerably more entertaining. Booking sequence for a lunch charter Pick a route from the table above and message us the date on WhatsApp via the homepage . We hold the boat for 24 hours while you reserve the restaurant directly. Send us the reservation confirmation; we plan timings around the table slot. Pay a 30% deposit to confirm; balance settles on the day in Puerto Banús. Arrive 15 minutes before departure at the Levante quay; the skipper greets you with the drinks already on ice. Frequently asked questions Which Marbella restaurants can I actually arrive at by boat? You can reach Puerto Banús quayside venues (Cipriani, La Sala by the Sea, Astral) directly by mooring stern-to. For beach clubs like Nikki Beach, Trocadero Arena, Bono Beach and the Cabopino chiringuitos, you anchor 100m off the sand and our skipper runs you in by tender. Plan a 1-2NM hop from Puerto Banús — most stops are 10-20 minutes away. Do I need to book a berth in Puerto Banús for lunch? For our fleet under 15m, the skipper handles same-day berthing via VHF 09 on arrival; usually you get a slot within 20 minutes. For yachts over 20m (Mangusta 80, Canados 86, Ferretti 94) we pre-book the day before. Lunch-only stays of 2-3 hours are charged at the short-stay quayside rate, typically €40-€90 depending on length overall. How does a tender drop-off at a beach club work? Your skipper anchors 80-150m off the beach in 4-6m of water, then ferries guests ashore in the tender, two or three at a time. You step off in knee-deep water onto the sand and walk 30 seconds to the chiringuito. Bags, phones and shoes ride in a dry bag. The skipper waits aboard and collects you when you signal by phone or VHF. What is the dress code at Marbella beachfront restaurants? Chiringuitos like Trocadero Arena, Bono Beach and the Cabopino huts are swimwear-friendly at lunch — sarong or shirt over your costume is fine. Puerto Banús quayside venues (Cipriani, Astral) expect smart-casual: linen shirts, dresses, dry shoes. Nikki Beach enforces no swimwear at the table after 14:00, so pack a change of clothes if that is your stop. Can we eat onboard instead of going ashore? Yes — every charter includes water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava and light snacks. For a full meal we can pre-order catering: tapas platters from €18 per person, sushi boxes around €35, or a paella delivered to the boat for €45 per head. Tell us the day before and we collect the order from Puerto Banús before departure. Drinks remain included on top. What is the best route for a half-day lunch charter? From Puerto Banús, head east to Río Verde for a quick swim, anchor off Trocadero Arena (1.5NM, 12 minutes), eat lunch, then continue to Cabopino dunes (another 6NM east) for an afternoon swim before returning. Total distance about 16NM round-trip, comfortably done in a 4h Tier A charter at €749 or in 6h for a more relaxed pace. Are children welcome at these restaurants? Most chiringuitos are family-friendly — Bono Beach and the Cabopino huts have shaded play areas and kids' menus around €12-€16. Trocadero Arena and Nikki Beach accept children at lunchtime but lean adult. Puerto Banús venues like Cipriani are fine for over-eights but not really set up for toddlers. Home › Guide › Marbella Snorkeling Tour by Boat: Best Coves and Gear Tips By Andra Kiirkivi Founder & CEO · Boat Rental Marbella · Updated 20 May 2026 · Reviewed by local Marbella skippers Marbella's coastline hides some of the Costa del Sol's best snorkeling spots, and the best way to reach them is by private boat. A marbella snorkeling tour by boat lets you access secluded coves that are otherwise unreachable by land, with crystal-clear water, rocky reefs, and abundant marine life. Whether you're a first-timer or a seasoned snorkeller, this guide covers the top locations, what gear to bring, and how to book your trip from Puerto Banús. Why Choose a Boat for Snorkeling in Marbella? The beaches around Marbella are mostly sandy and shallow, but the best snorkeling happens near rocky headlands and coves. A private boat from Puerto Banús gives you direct access to spots like Cala del Faro and Cala Cortés, where visibility often reaches 15–20 metres on calm days. You avoid crowded shorelines, and your skipper anchors close to the rocks where fish gather. All our charters include a licensed skipper who knows the best spots based on wind and swell conditions. Best Coves for Snorkeling on a Marbella Boat Tour Here are the top coves our skippers recommend: Cala del Faro – Near Cabopino, this rocky cove has a small sandy beach and clear water with plenty of fish around the rocks. Depth ranges from 2 to 8 metres. Cala Cortés – West of Marbella, this sheltered cove offers calm water and a mix of sand and rock seabeds. Good for beginners. Punta de la Mona – A rocky headland with deeper water (up to 12 metres) and occasional sightings of stingrays and octopus. Cabopino Reef – Just off the Cabopino marina, this artificial reef attracts bream, wrasse, and small groupers. All these spots are within 30 minutes of Puerto Banús. Our skippers adjust the itinerary based on sea conditions and your preferences. Snorkeling Gear: What's Included and What to Bring We provide basic snorkeling masks and fins on every charter. For a more comfortable experience, we recommend bringing your own gear – especially if you need prescription lenses or prefer a dry snorkel. If you want to capture the underwater life, a GoPro or waterproof phone case is ideal. We also suggest a rash vest or UV shirt to protect against the strong Andalusian sun (SPF 50+ reef-safe sunscreen is essential). Avoid spray sunscreens, as they can harm marine life. Our Fleet: Which Boat Suits Your Snorkeling Trip? We have boats for every group size. For a small group of up to 5 guests, the Dubhe (8m) or Mariah SX21 (6.4m) are nimble and easy to anchor in tight coves. For up to 10 guests, the Fairline Targa 12m or Lagoon 380 catamaran offer stable platforms for snorkeling. For larger groups (up to 12), the Mangusta 80 (24m) includes a free jet ski, which is great for exploring shallower areas. All boats depart from Puerto Banús and include a licensed skipper, fuel, drinks, and snacks. Pricing for Snorkeling Charters Our most popular options for snorkeling tours are the Astondoa 40 and Azimut 39 , both from €749 for 2 hours or €2,299 for 8 hours (includes skipper, drinks, and VAT). The Mangusta 80 (available in grey or white) starts at €4,719 for a minimum 4 hours and includes a free jet ski. For other boats like the Ferretti 94 or Canados 86 , pricing is on request via WhatsApp. All prices include 21% Spanish IVA, fuel, insurance, and a full drinks and snacks package. What to Expect During Your Snorkeling Tour Your skipper will welcome you at Puerto Banús and brief you on the day's plan. After a short cruise (10–30 minutes) to your chosen cove, the skipper anchors and you can jump in from the swim platform. Snorkeling sessions typically last 30–45 minutes per cove. Between swims, you can relax on deck, enjoy drinks (water, soft drinks, beer, white wine, cava), and light snacks. Most 4-hour tours visit 2–3 coves. For the best experience, book a full-day (8-hour) charter to explore further afield, including spots near Estepona or Sotogrande. Best Months for Snorkeling in Marbella Water temperatures peak from June to October, reaching 24–26°C in August. Visibility is best in July and August, often exceeding 15 metres. Spring (April–May) and autumn (September–October) are also good, with fewer crowds and water temperatures around 18–22°C. Winter months (November–March) are cooler (14–17°C) but still possible with a wetsuit (we can provide one on request). Book Your Marbella Snorkeling Tour by Boat Ready to explore the underwater world of the Costa del Sol? Browse our full fleet on the Boat Rental Marbella page, or contact us via WhatsApp for a personalised recommendation. We'll help you choose the perfect boat and cove for your snorkeling adventure. Frequently asked questions What is the best time of year for a marbella snorkeling tour by boat? The best months are June through October, when water temperatures range from 20°C to 26°C. July and August offer the calmest seas and best visibility, often exceeding 15 metres. Spring and autumn can also be good, but expect cooler water and more variable conditions. Which coves are included in a marbella snorkeling tour by boat? Popular coves include Cala del Faro (near Cabopino), Cala Cortés (west of Marbella), and the rocky areas around Punta de la Mona. All are within a 30-minute cruise from Puerto Banús. Our skippers know the calmest spots based on wind and swell. Do you provide snorkeling gear on the boat? Yes, we supply basic snorkeling masks and fins on all charters. For higher-quality gear or prescription masks, we recommend bringing your own. We also have a selection of GoPro mounts available upon request. Can beginners join a marbella snorkeling tour by boat? Absolutely. Our skippers provide a quick safety briefing and choose calm, shallow coves ideal for beginners. Life jackets are available. Many of our guests have never snorkelled before and enjoy spotting fish right from the swim platform. What marine life can I expect to see? Common sightings include damselfish, wrasse, bream, and occasional octopus. In deeper areas near Cabopino, you may see small stingrays or sea turtles. The rocky seabeds around Cala del Faro are home to colourful algae and starfish. How long should I book for a snorkeling-focused charter? We recommend at least 4 hours. This allows time to cruise to two or three coves, spend 30–45 minutes snorkelling at each, and enjoy lunch or drinks onboard. Shorter 2-hour trips work for a single cove if you're short on time. What should I bring for a marbella snorkeling tour by boat? Bring a towel, reef-safe sunscreen (non-spray to avoid damaging marine life), a rash vest or UV shirt, a hat, and a waterproof phone case. A GoPro or underwater camera is great for memories. We provide drinks and snacks. Can I combine snorkeling with other activities on the tour? Yes. Many guests combine snorkeling with paddleboarding (available on request), jet skiing (free on Mangusta 80 charters), or simply sunbathing on deck.
